# 295\n
{London, British Library, Cotton Vespasian A.iii, hand A: Cursor Mundi etc}\n
C14\n
388 447 N\n
{=WRY=}\n
{=Script - a rather stiff Textura, see below=}\n
{=Sample tagged: fols. 2ra-10vb. Hand A writes fols. 2r-91v; 93va line\n
9-95vb line 19; 99ra-112vb; 119rb-139va line 36 Cursor Mundi and fols.\n
139va line 37-163ra: Exposition of the Creed, Lord\'s Prayer and\n
Exposition, Prayer for the Hours of the Passion, Prayer to the\n
Trinity, The Book of Penance=}\n
{=Hand A is a rather stiff Textura which is very difficult to date.\n
Wright (1960: 11) gives it a date of \'about A.D. 1340\', and Hupe\n
(1893: 63*) puts all three hands in the early 14th century. In a\n
later essay (same vol. pp. 124-25) he goes back on this and assigns\n
all three hands \'to the same time\' but says that Scribe A belongs to\n
the 14th century and Scribes B and C to the 15th, Scribe A being\n
therefore necessarily an old man at the time of writing. Hands B and C\n
are certainly at least as late as late 14th century and probably into\n
the 15th - both are cursive Anglicana. Hand C also displays some\n
secretary features. This would imply that Scribe A, whose work on\n
fol. 119rb follows straight on from that of Scribe C on fol. 119ra,\n
was probably working later than the first half of the 14th century\n
also, which would render his contribution technically too late for\n
inclusion in LAEME. But in view of the earlier dating in Wright I\n
have tagged some of his text as possibly representative of Northern\n
usage of the first half of the 14th century=}\n
{=Status - MS punctuation done; tagging notes and textual notes up to date=}\n
{~f2ra~}\n
{>}\n
{=ins, in top margin, a hand with pointing index finger followed by\n
heading and other entries running into the right hand margin, in hands\n
later than that of the scribe of the text=}\n
{)\'*THE *CURSUR OF THE WORLD\')}\n
{([illeg] \\ (PAGINE PAT( \\ *VESPASIAN \\ *A3(}\n
{>}\n
{=Y is used for thorn throughout. Morris EETS OS 57 (1857) adds\n
editorial punctuation which I do not reproduce here. MS punctuation\n
rarely occurs. I have included what I can see on the microfilm -\n
mostly midline raised punctus which I do not differentiate from\n
punctus on the base line. Occasionally rhyming couplets are joined\n
by braces, but there seems no system to this and I have not noted them=}\n

{=Chertsey, N Surrey=}\n
{=Sample represents all the continuous text in English in this hand.\n
There are boundary clauses in English in the same hand on fols. 21v-23r\n
and 36v-37r=}\n
{=Script - proto-Gothic book-hand=}\n
{=Status - MS punctuation done; tagging notes and textual notes up to date=}\n
{=Punctuation is confined to the punctus. Sometimes this appears joined\n
to the last stroke of the previous letter (most often T or E) and may\n
sometimes therefore be a resting of the pen rather than a deliberate\n
mark of punctuation. But its appearance is most often in natural\n
pausing places and dividing words in a list, so even when they touch\n
the ending of the preceding letter I have recorded such dots as punctus=}\n
{~f50r~}\n

{=N Gloucs=}\n
{=Sample represents all the text in English in this hand=}\n
{=Script - proto-Gothic book hand with some Anglicana features, but not\n
a cursive hand=}\n
{=Status - MS punctuation done; tagging notes and textual notes up to date=}\n
{=MS badly damaged by the Cottonian fire. Only 451 lines remain, only\n
180 completely legible. Readings that are uncertain, incomplete or\n
whose context is insufficient to make sense of the syntax even with\n
reference to other versions of the text, have been placed in braces.\n
The text is adapted from Lumby\'s (re-edited McKnight) EETS OS 14 (1866),\n
transcript,  corrected from an inadequate photocopy of the original.\n
The whole should be checked again from the original if possible. I\n
believe more corrections to Lumby\'s text may be possible. In order to\n
make the present text readable I have supplied the sense of the missing\n
text, based {on the parallel Trentham MS text in EETS OS 14. Where the\n
text is not fully parallel, I have conjectured the substance of the\n
missing text wherever it is sufficiently clear from the context.\n
Elsewhere, missing text is indicated by dots (corresponding to those\n
supplied by Lumby) placed in brackets=}\n
